  41. I bought this to replace a Panasonic wet-dry shaver with linear motor. I'm pleased with the way it works; even though it does not shave quite as close as the Panasonic, it's far more comfortable.   54. I've used this shaver for a few weeks now and am very impressed. In fact, I'm so impressed I just purchased a second one last night for my travel bag I keep with me in my car. I only use it wet with Edge Ultra Sensitive Shave Gel after wetting my face with water as from past experience with other electric shavers that always provides for a far superior shave, hence why I wanted this wet/dry shaver. If you've never tried a wet electric shave, have tough to cut hair, and you shave near a sink, I highly recommend trying it. I haven't tried this shaver dry, so I can not comment on its dry performance. I primarily use this shaver for my upper lip and the area around my chin, my upper neck (which it still does an amazing job with), and lips since my hair grows even tougher in these areas, they're hard to shave on, and I often end up gashing myself if I use a regular blade. I do find I have to push pretty hard to get a close shave, and I'm wondering what that's going to do to the life of the foil/cutters, but at least this shaver has yet to nick me! As with other electric shavers (and to a lesser extend blades even), it may take up to 5-10 passes over my skin to cut my hair thoroughly, and I also make sure I pull/stretch my skin against the direction my hair grows in so that my hair pops out more off my skin. I still use a blade in combination with this (Gillette Fusion Proglide Power) on the rest of my face, and for touching up. I've tried many electric shavers in the past - Braun, Norelco, Remington, Panasonic, and Sanyo shavers and they've all let me down, draining me of thousands of dollars. I had been previously using a Sanyo SV-RX10 shaver for several years that I purchased several of since it was the best of the wet/dry shavers that I tried that would even semi-work with my thick tough hair. Unfortunately though I had two of them that just died, the foil/cutter assembly didn't last long, and the shaver itself was cheaper than getting the replacement foil/cutter assembly from only one of two sources that sold it! I was hesitant to try a Braun again due to a bad experience with one of their higher end shavers in the $200 range that I ended up returning. It was so loud it would wake up the entire house and I would have had a better shave running the edge of a pair of scissors down my face. This Braun 380S-4 not only does an even superior job to the Sanyo I liked, but it's also far quieter than the Sanyo as well as the previous Braun I tried, while still having lots of power in the motor. Not only is the motor and blade motion quieter, but when I first used it I didn't even think it was cutting my hair at all since with other electric shavers I've been able to hear them cut my hair. It also comes with a nice travel case, though there isn't space in it to hold the charger unfortunately. My only concern so far with the Braun 380S-4 is the replacement foil/cutter (apparently part number 32s/b) that is available as of writing this is not of the same design (at least the foil) as included with the 380S-4 new. So, I'm hoping the older design will be discontinued soon in favor of the foil design on this shaver with regular circular holes instead of the random sized/shaped holes on the older design that doesn't let my hair through. I can't comment on extended use and the life of the foil/cutter assembly (which is always a gross exaggeration by manufacturers) since I haven't had it long enough to even charge a second time, but I might update this review at a later date when I can provide some more feedback. One last note: you can find additional reviews on Amazon's UK site (amazon.co.uk). This is where I read the inital reviews for this shaver since there was only a couple here at the time I purchased this.

  68. UPDATE, November 2015 I gave this razor/shaver 4 stars when I first reviewed it. I'm dropping that to three, and have considered dropping it to two stars. Why: the cutter head became unusably dull after less than six months use, as opposed to the 18 months that it is claimed to last. I tried to buy a replacement cutter head, but found them out of stock everywhere, despite many vendors selling on Amazon claiming that they were in stock. This is a significant problem to the man who needs to shave every day and doesn't want to pull his beard out by the roots for any longer than necessary. Further, a new Braun cutter assembly has always, previously, restored the performance to nearly new. The new cutter that I finally bought did nothing of the sort. It's better than the old one, but significantly inferior to the original that came with the shaver. See update at end of the review for a more pungent analysis. ----------------------------- I bought my first Braun in Germany around 1966. Plug in only; no battery; no recharging; and very sensitive to the frequency of the alternating current (I had to change a spring when I got back to the US). But solid, rugged as the dickens. And it gave such a close shave that for many months I had to dig out ingrown hairs from my beard. Lasted about six years until I just wanted a rechargeable model. I've had a bunch of Brauns over the years. Until Procter and Gamble bought them from Gillette, which had bought the whole company many years back, Brauns were superb. Since then some have been gimmicky and downright fragile. Others pretty good. I wanted to change brands in protest against the wretched customer service two years ago, and bought a Norelco 3D 3-head rotary shaver. It had a number of design problems which made it less useful (the teensy sideburn trimmer, for example). I finally needed a third cutting head (one spare came in the package), and clicked on Amazon to buy it. Surprise. They had redesigned the assembly, cheapened the design, and made such a poor one that most Amazon commenters down checked it severely. Not wanting to shave with that, I decided to try Braun again and thought the 380S-4 was pretty neat, esp. at last week's $69 price. This shaver is a nice friendly shape, with confidence inspiring solidity and a nice hand position. At least the first few shaves left my cheeks baby-smooth, and that lasted for about 14 hours before getting a bit sandpapery. The sideburn trimmer is well designed for the job of cleaning up really long hair that sometimes grows on my lower neck. The shaves were quick too; just 2-3 minutes for a whole face (shaving with 'Lectric Shave prep). Some have been a bit dubious about the foil lock switch on the razor. I'm not; I love it. I have very sensitive skin and very tough whiskers under my nose and beneath my mouth. With the lock &#34;on&#34;, it gets those whiskers with one pass; my late (and now unlamented) Norelco failed that test completely. I had to use the teensy pop-out trimmer which really doesn't work well. All in all I'm pretty pleased with the 380S-4. Time will tell about battery and cutter assembly life. For that you need about a year of shaving. I do hope I'll never need customer &#34;service.&#34; I'll update when I have more information. UPDATE:....... I've owned the shaver since last spring, roughly April. The &#34;18 month&#34; lifetime for the cutter assembly is a joke. By early Novemer I was in the hunt for a new cutter. A joke, that. None of the Amazon dealers had it in stock. Several said &#34;in stock&#34; but each of those said not in stock or back ordered when I tried to buy one. The maker refused to sell me one directly, although they did send me a gift card for $30 to make up for the laughably short blade life. A routine check of Amazon a few weeks later showed one dealer who did have the cutter and would sell it to me, and actually did deliver. Surprise! That didn't restore the originalperformance as advertised. (Did you think it would?) I don't want to spend the bucks for a new shaver, so will endure the poor shaves and pulling of hair and burning of cheeks for at least a bit longer. The new cutter did improve things quite a bit, but not enough to satisfy. I got the distinct feeling the model could be being discontinued shortly since cutters were in short supply. Another update: ============ I've been shaving with the new cutter for a couple of months. It pulls hairs a lot and doesn't shave as close as it did the day I got it. The power of the shaver motor seems less than it was. We're this a cheap shaver I would just toss it. But it is not. I guess &#34;Braun&#34; isn't the Braun of old. I would save my money and look for some other maker of foil shavers; I do prefer them to rotary mechanisms. Originally I gave this shaver a lot of stars; in view of the short lifetime and the difficulty of finding parts and service, I'm degrading it to two stars and will keep monitoring that until I settle on a replacement. ================= Update, February 2016. The motor is slowing a bit. Even the new cutting head and foil didn't work very well. It's pulling beard hairs all the time, and my face is complaining. The higher line Brauns are getting ferociously expensive. Does anyone have any suggestions for brands and models. I have to change razors pretty darn soon. What about the Panasonic ARC 3 or 4?

I chose the 380S-4 for two reasons: 1) user reviews indicate it shaves well and 2) uniquely among Braun shavers it is set up for travel (I have a couple of trips each year that take me away from home for about a month). For most purposes the actual shaver is no different than Braun's 340S-4 (there is an extra charge indicator light and a \\"precision setting switch\\" that lifts one of the heads to better shave under your nose - in my estimation neither of these is a significant enhancement). Unless you just want Braun's travel case, I suggest you go with the 340 and save yourself $20 (the 340 has a plastic clip on hood to protect the shaver head, and so should also be travel worthy in an after market case).<br /><br />As a shaver the performance is impressive, a bit of an improvement over the 7505 and in operation the unit is considerably quieter. I'm finding it to do a better job of getting pesky neck hairs and am able to achieve a better outcome overall without any significant skin irritation (and I have fairly sensitive skin). My beard is moderate and I shave daily, so take that into consideration. Also I only \\"dry\\" shave, although the unit is designed for wet or dry shaving. The 7505 required periodic cleaning of its blade assembly with a brush. For this model, the blade assembly and foil are integrated and so can only be truly cleaned by rinsing under running water. Since I live in a hard water region, I'll be curious to see how it holds up to the mineral assault. The unit has a light that won't come on until it is time for a new cutter head assembly but it is simple minded (a internal countertriggers the light, presumably around 18 months - it is easily reset by pressing in the on/off switch for 5 seconds; i.e., the unit can't actually tell whether or not the head needs replacing).<br /><br />One downside is that the unit only operates off of battery, but supposedly can charge sufficiently in 5 minutes for a single shave (I suspect that since the shaver is designed to be used wet/dry, Braun decided that if configured to operate corded, some idiot might choose to use it that way while in the shower). My only real beef is that the travel case supplied with this model has no means for accommodating the power cord, although it is very well designed to protect the shaver.<br /><br />7/1/2012 update: I've actually become more impressed with this shaver. Not only is it holding up under my hard water assault, but it has an interesting feature not otherwise mentioned. Namely, the power circuit uses a voltage regulator so the unit runs at the same speed regardless of the amount of charge on the battery. For this reason, it quits rather abruptly as it is draining the last bit of juice out of the battery (this kind of technology is used in good quality LED flashlights and will fully drain the typical AA alkaline battery without any loss of light output until the battery is kaput). This is precisely the reason a 5 minute charge is sall that is needed to put enough juice back in the battery for a shave. That's a really nice feature. One other thing. I noted that over time a haze of very fine grit accumulates which rinsing doesn't remove, but it is easily cleared by using a can of compressed air, something I'm surprised Braun doesn't suggest when you want to completely return the shaver to like new appearance.<br /><br />8/29/2012 update: One more thing, when it becomes time to get a replacement head be aware that Braun has several types of Series 3 shavers and the heads are not cross-compatible. The replacement for this one is either Series 3 32S (silver trim) or Series 3 32B (black trim), whatever your color preference (I would just pick whichever is cheaper).

It's very easy to care for this quickly and efficiently (it's a Braun, what would you expect?). Pop the shaver into the provided small stand to keep it out of the way until the next day. The shaver can charge on that stand as well when the time comes; just plug in the charging cord on the receptacle on the stand and you can see when the shaver is fully charged. Another minor thing - you can't just plug the cord in and shave, as the shaver does not work while in charging mode. But you can do a quick charge, enough to shave that day, in about 5 minutes, and then you can do a full recharge in just over an hour.<br /><br />So if you are looking for a very good shaver on a smaller budget but don't want to sacrifice quality, I would urge you toconsider this model very seriously.

  255. My wife gave me this shaver for Christmas. Now I’ve tried it out thoroughly. I like it a lot.<br /><br />The cons are as other reviewers have said: (1) it takes longer to shave than with a blade; (2) the shave you get isn’t as close, and (3) it takes two weeks or more to get used to shaving electrically if you aren’t already. On long days you can get a five-o’clock shadow.<br /><br />But for me, this shaver has four decisive advantages. First, it doesn’t pull long hairs or pinch skin like the electric I had when I last tried one some thirty years ago.<br /><br />Second, it lets you stand up straight while you shave, instead of bending over a sink. For someone my age (68) with a tricky back, that’s a crucial advantage.<br /><br />Third, unlike a blade, it shaves the tricky parts without cutting you, every time. Between bending over and cutting myself, I had come to hate shaving so much that I wouldn’t do it on days I didn’t leave the house. Now I don’t mind shaving and have made it an every-morning routine.<br /><br />Fourth, I hated being beholden to Gillette for blades, to the tune of about $1.50 per day. It’s not just the money, which really isn’t that much, but the constant worry about running out of blades and reordering. Now, according to the instructions, I can take shaving for granted for 180 days.<br /><br />I read all the instructions and followed them carefully. In particular, I discharged the shaver completely twice, to avoid problems with battery memory. While I did so, I got over a week's worth of shaves with no power at all. Then I still had a bright red light which (according to the instructions) means you can finish your shave.<br /><br />This is a great product at a great price.

  366. Summary: Although this is far less expensive than the Braun 5 or 7 Series razors, it holds its own and stands out as Braun's only wet-capable shaver. I found it provided a better wet shave than my Panasonic ArcIV, Norelco AT830, and Norelco Sensotouch 3D.<br /><br />Main review: I'm a big Braun fan, and have been a 5 and 7 series user for a number of years (before they were called the 5 and 7 series). I've always been impressed by their performance and build quality. However, I've recently started to prefer a wet shave and thought it would be interesting to give a Braun wet shaver a spin.<br /><br />Very pleased that I did. This is absolutely the best wet shave I've ever had bar none, and a very good dry shave as well.<br /><br />My other wet shavers are the Panasonic ArcIV, the Norelco AT830, and the Norelco Sensotouch 3D. The Braun 380s beats them all.<br /><br />Of the three, the Panny comes the closest to the Braun's overall comfort performance, but the Braun wins out by not leaving any rough patches on the jaw line and neck areas. The Norelcos perform well on my neck and jaw line, but you need multiple passes which often leave me with some irritation and redness. The Braun, in contrast, is very gentle but still manages to provide a close shave.<br /><br />I got the best shave using a thin gel such as this:[[ASIN:B005ACNP5K Remington King of Shaves Alphagel Cooling Menthol Shave Gel 5 oz. (Pack of 2)]] ). You can see where you are cutting, and there's very little mess.<br /><br />I'm particularly impressed with the build quality of the 380s. Both my 5 and 7 Series are made in Germany, so this is my first made in China Braun. Regardless of where it was made, it's put together very well - feels solid and has the good heft Braun's are known for. Right before I got the 380s I was evaluating a Remington FR-750, which (at the time I'm writing this in July 2012) is priced exactly the same as the 380s on Amazon. What a huge build quality gap! As I noted in my FR-750 review, the Remington felt rather cheap. Compared with the 380s, it feels like a Cracker Jack toy. And it's the same price!<br /><br />The 380s has many design cues from the 5 Series. It's about the same length but a bit wider. It feels comfortable to hold due to a rubber, non-slip grip. It also has one of my favorite 5 Series features: a push up trimmer. This is the best way to edge a mustache since you can see exactly where you are cutting, and is much easier to maneuver than a flip out trimmer.<br /><br />This does not have a cleaning base like most of the 5 and 7 Series models. Although the cleaning bases work very well, it's not a big loss since for the 380s since it's easy to clean under running water.<br /><br />It does have a stand, which connects to the cord so it charges when it's put back in the stand. Although the stand is small, it has a non-slip base so it's generally sturdy. I would have liked to see a bigger base, however, for a more secure hold onto the razor.<br /><br />If you are a Braun user and want to shave wet, but don't want to give up the feel of a Braun shave, this is a no-brainer purchase. Either get the 380s (this model) or the 340s. The only things you give up with the 340 is the display (slight more fancy in the 380), a carry case, and the locking head (you can slide a switch and the front foil and middle bar get pushed down so you can more easily shave tight spots such as under your nose. Not terribly useful, but it has some benefits). If the prices are about the same spring for the 380 if only for the carry case. If you can get a deal on the 340 go for that. The shave is the same for both.<br /><br />But even if you only want to shave dry, don't skip the 3 Series in favor of the more popular 5 and 7 Series. Yes, the 7 Series is still my all-time favorite foil. But while it does provide a closer shave than a 3 Series, the difference is not huge. Unless you're really fussy about the quality of shave you get, or are a shaver nut like I am,save the bucks and get a 3 Series.<br /><br />The 3 Series is the clear choice over the 5 Series. Both are identical in terms of the shave quality, both have a wonderful push-up trimmer; both are comfortable and well-built. The 5 series is put together better, with more metal and less plastic. It also has a narrower head, which comes in handy in the tight spots. But given the cost difference, the 3 Series is the better choice. Plus, the 380/340 has a more flexible foil design which I find offers better cutting in less time than the 5 series.<br /><br />Lastly, if you're a confirmed dry shave fan, give wet shaving a try. If you use the right gel, it can be nearly as mess-free and quick as a dry shave, but will give you a closer, more gentle shave.<br /><br />Happy shaving!<br /><br />PS: The proper replacement head for the 340/380 is either the 32s or the 32b. Both are the same, with the only difference being color (silver or black).save the bucks and get a 3 Series.<br /><br />The 3 Series is the clear choice over the 5 Series. I've timed the battery life on two occasions and total shaving time comes to 45 minutes on a full charge. There are two green lights that stay on when the shaver is charged. As the battery drains the lights go out one at a time. The first green light goes out at approximately 13 minutes. The second one goes out and the red blinking light comes on after 31 minutes. I was able to continue shaving for an average of 13-14 minutes after the red light started blinking. The only comment I would make, would be it would be nice if you could shave while the shaver was charging. If it stops, you have to plug it in and wait 5 minutes or so before you can finish your shave. For me, the 45 minutes allows me to recharge the shaver about every two weeks.<br /><br />UPDATE: 12/19/2012<br />I've had the shaver for over 1 year now and still happy with it. Battery life is still pretty good. I didn't let the battery run down all the way, but I've used it for two weeks without charging and a total of 42 1/2 minutes of use. After the red light comes on you still have about 12-13 minutes of use. I bought an extra shaving cassette to have on hand, but shaving is still close, quiet and comfortable.<br /><br />Update: 01/04/2014<br />Still like the Braun Shaver after two years. Battery life a little shorter but still good for almost two weeks. Here is a table of run time:<br /><br />Braun Shaver - Purchased 12/14/2011<br /><br />Date............1st Light.......Red Light.......Total Time.......Time after red light<br /><br />01/01/12.........13.00...........32.75...........46.50...............13.50<br /><br />07/19/12.........13.50...........31.00...........45.50...............14.50<br /><br />12/19/12.........12.00...........28.00...........40.75...............12.75<br /><br />07/01/13.........12.00...........30.00...........43.50...............13.50<br /><br />12/04/13.........11.50...........28.00...........42.00...............14.00<br /><br />Update 06/27/2014:<br /><br />In spite of what tph1983 thinks, I'm not psychotic nor am I am employee of Braun. I hope my review is helpful. Battery life is important, especially when this particular shaver will only run on battery and not with the cord plugged in. After two and a half years, the battery still runs for approximately two weeks (average 3 minutes/day) and a total of 42 minutes before it totally runs out of power. I prefer foil shavers to Norelco rotary and I like the wet shaving experience. If those two things are important to you, look no further.<br /><br />I bought mine because my Panasonic ES quit working after less than a year. There are not many wet-dry foil alternatives to the aggravating Panasonic shavers. But this one is better in just about every way.<br /><br />The Braun shaves about as close as an electric can. That's not because of a pivoting head or multiple motors: It's because the blades are sized for maneuverability and the the shaver fits well in your hand. These are some of the other things that I consider major plusses:<br /><br />1. The indicator lights tell you how much battery charge is left. But there are no fancy icons telling you when to clean the shaver. And no numbers telling you how many minutes a shave lasted. I think simpler is better-- fewer digital features means fewer things to malfunction.<br /><br />2. The \\"on\\" switch is located in a position that makes it very difficult to accidentally turn on when traveling. At first, I wished for a \\"travel lock\\" feature like you'll find on many Norelcos and Panasonics. But the positioning of the switch makes that unnecessary.<br /><br />3. Unlike other Brauns, you're not forced to use a cleaning system that requires expensive refills. This shaver is very easy to clean with your own alcohol.<br /><br />If you love technology and care about advanced electronics or cleaning systems, this Braun probably isn't for you. But if your priority is getting a great shave, the 380S-4 won't disappoint.<br /><br />UPDATE: I prefer wet shaving and have used various creams, soaps, and foams. These were nearly impossible to clean out of the cheap plastic parts inside the shaver. Every plastic part is crammed tightly into a space that cannot be reached. While attempting to cleanthese nooks with alcohol and a toothbrush, I managed to break two of the parts that were corroded and caked with soap residue.<br /><br />The bottom line: Braun built its reputation on dry electric shavers and is relatively new to wet-dry technology. I believe that this is their only wet-dry model at the time I am writing. It's a decent foil shaver if you only use it dry. But if you use it wet, you'll find it very difficult to clean and maintain. The plastic is cheap Chinese mass production at its worst. If you want quality wet-dry electric shaving, look at other brands.

I've found the best way to clean it is to remove the screen/cutters from the shaver, tap it on the side of the sink to make the beard particles fall out, then flush it with hot water under the faucet until the remaining beard particles come out. Only the recommended 32s or 32b will fit as per the owners manual.<br /><br />Update June 11, 2013: Just wanted to let you all know the screen finally developed a hole in it this morning, so the life of the screen/cutter assembly was about 2-1/2 months. Useage conditions were not as a wet shaver as can be done with this model, but using standard method, i.e., Williams Electric shave lotion as lubricant and rinsing the screen under hot water until all the particles come out.

  407. This is my first electric razor in years. I will start by saying that your skin does really adapt to the razor over the first couple of weeks. Now that the razor and I have grown accustomed to each other, I can feel stubble when rubbing my neck against the grain on a couple of neck areas, such as the Adams apple, but cannot see it after shaving. One plus is that I no longer get ingrown hairs after switching from a blade to this razor. This is a caveat of the electric razor, and one I can live with. It does not miss hairs and I have a very thick beard. I do recommend trimming your hair with the built in trimmer if it gets long from not shaving, as it will pull hairs that are approx 1/8 of an inch or longer. The trimmer is also precise for edging up a goatee or sideburns. I wear a fumanchu and find it very easy to get the foil up to the edge to shave all the hair. I have sensitive skin and experience no irritation at all, but I do use a face lotion after I shave. It is very easy to clean and can be dry brushed or rinsed out. I prefer dry brushing so I don't have to lubricate it as often.

  510. Like many of you here browsing these reviews you are torn between shavers and razors. I thought my friend was full of it but since he is normally a pretty straight guy I thought I'd do my own research into it. He suggested checking out a Braun shaver in the mid-$200 range.<br /><br />I wasn't exactly how much I wanted to drop over $200 on a razor but it got me thinking. So like many of you I started reading all the reviews. I read so much junk that I was overloaded by info. One overriding impression I had was that newer electric shavers have come a long way. So I decided to bite the bullet and buy one. Again I didn't want to spend a fortune but wanted a good enough one that it would be representative of what they have to offer.<br /><br />What really pushed me into the electric shaver test was a recent international trip. I was in a country that didn't seem to have any warm/hot water with any frequency and I can't shave without it. I had already suffered through a number of cold shaves to the point that I wanted another option and the electric shaver seemed like a good one. I also thought that maybe if this razor didn't cut it (pun intended) so to speak that maybe the Series 7 or a Panasonic might.<br /><br />OTOH I love shaving when I am in the shower. So I started to explore the wet-dry options out there. I ultimately ended up with the Braun 380S-4. I searched around and found one locally. I really was set on the 340 but I scored a great deal on the 380 and glad I have the case the precision trimmer option for close to the nose shaving.<br /><br />All this doesn't really matter if when the rubber hits the road (or shaver hits the beard in this case) and nothing works as planned. In this respect I am totally surprised. During my research I saw some videos on the best way to use the shaver such as, don't wash my face (if dry shaving, to pretreat with something like William's Lectric Shave (waited a few minutes after applying though), etc. I did all these things and amazingly I got a very good shave.<br /><br />One thing I would stress from anyone going to an electric shaver from a razor is you may have hit your hair from different angles to find the best cutting stroke. In some areas it took me 2 passes to find the best way to shave an area. I would say electric shavers might be more sensitive to the \\"grain\\" of your hair. I have a pretty heavy beard and have 5 o'clock shadow if I shave at 6 or 7 in the morning with a good normal razor. The 2 blade throw-aways basically give me 11am shadow, it didn't even wait until 5 o'clock.<br /><br />So imagine my surprise when at the end of the workday my face looked just as good as my normal razor. I was totally amazed to say the least. Quite honestly the shave from the 380 might have even been slightly better. The day before I shaved with my normal razor and now I am into my first week of shaving with just the shaver. My face hasn't broken out anywhere. All in all I am virtually ecstatic. I honestly can't see spending the extra $$$ on the Series 7 yet as my expectations so far have been exceeded. I might try it just to see if it is really any better. I think with time I'll get an even better shave once I use it for a while. I haven't had a chance to shave with it wet yet but so far I have no buyer's remorse.<br /><br />One other thing I started to think about. While the Gilette Fusion Proglide blades worked great for me, they are expensive. I was considering shaving clubs and the like. I normally got maybe a week to 10 days out of a blade. I was going through about 30 or so a year. It won't take long for me to come out ahead financially with the Braun and even soon when I factor in some other grooming I did with blades. Just to shave my chest and stomach would use an entire Fusion blade! In less than a year I'llbe ahead not even factoring in the hot water I can save by not shaving in the shower. The 2-3 minute of hot water would add up in both water and energy costs as well.<br /><br />All in all I am glad I took the gamble. I'll report back in a month or so. For me the extra cost for the 380 over the 340 was worth having the case, more intelligent battery display (business trips) and the precision trimmer lock. If I was going to be over $100 I would have seriously looked at the Series 7 or Panasonic. Main reason I really didn't jump on the 7 was the lack of a wet shaving feature even though I haven't used it so far. It is nice to have the option.

  535. Let me start by saying that I recently switched back to electric shaving after many years of either not shaving or using a manual razor. Following the recommendation of Consumer Reports I tried the Panasonic 8103 so this review is a comparison of the Panasonic 8103 and the Braun 380.<br /><br />First off, the build quality of both are very good with the slight edge to the Braun with the slightly heavier feel and premium rubber handles on the side. The Panasonic, to me, looked pretty cheap only with the chrome accents. The Panasonic's shave head is very large and makes the unit look very top-heavy and the Braun about as streamlined as you can expect.<br /><br />The charging of the units was about the same in term of the time it takes to get a full charge (about 1 hour) but hands down the Braun holds a charge much longer than the Panny (I could get about 1 week of shaves with Panny and am consistently getting about 2 weeks with Braun). The only advantage the Panny has on charging is that it has a \\"cool\\" lcd display of the amount of charge left (i.e. 50%, 10%, etc). Both units do not allow you to shave and charge at the same time due to water/electrical hazard which is disappointing but understandable.<br /><br />The Braun 380 comes with what I would a term a very serviceable case (somewhat of a hard case with a Braun logo on the side). The Panny does not come with a case.<br /><br />The shaving experience is where I believe the Braun really shines through. I shave in the shower so have no idea how well this unit \\"dry\\" shaves. I use a clear King of Shaves gel so I can see where I am shaving and the Braun powers right through the water/gel combination with little to no resistance. The Panny also has very little resistance when shaving but misses a lot of whiskers under the chin (neck area) and is very average at shaving in the mustache area. The Braun may take a few extra strokes on the neck area but ultimately gets all the whiskers but is extremely impressive in the mustache area. I can manage a full shave in about 7-10 mins with the Braun and about 8-12 with the Panny (takes a lot more strokes).<br /><br />Clean up is identical other than Braun recommends the use of a supplied oil once/week if you clean your shaver under running water.<br /><br />The only complaint I have for both units is that I ultimately have to use a manual razor below the side burns to get a close shave and straight edge on the side burns. I, personally, like to have a very clean look on my extended side burns so this is not a huge inconvenience.<br /><br />In the end I think both units are great shavers but the slight edge to the Braun 380 for the reasons listed above. Braun has a 60 day satisfaction guarantee so I recommend trying the Braun out first so it gives you sufficient time to see if it's a fit. Panny does not have such a guarantee but you can certainly use the 30 day return policy with Amazon for a test period.<br /><br />Hope this helps.in the mustache area.   598. I have used mostly Norelco rotary shavers, but had heard that Braun was \\"the best\\". When my last rotary (a Remington) finally fell apart on me, I decided it was time to see if people were correct. I checked the Braun website, looking for their best model that did not include a cleaning system. I didn't want the extra equipment or cost of refill solution. The 380S-4 seemed to be the one I should try.<br /><br />First impression: This is a solid, apparently well-made shaver. There is some heft to it. It is easy to hold, with rubberized grip areas where one needs them. One simple button for on-off, one simple slide for the trimmer, the head assembly just pulls off and clicks on. The only gimmick is a slide that lowers one foil and the long-hair clipper, leaving one foil high for ease of 'precision' shaving. The charger cord either plugs in to the bottom of the shaver directly, or attaches to a small drop-in base. Seems to hold a charge for a long time, though I haven't timed it. I use it dry, can't comment on wet use.<br /><br />The good: The pop-up trimmer has to be the best I have ever seen on a general-purpose shaver. Maybe dedicated trimmers are better, I have no experience with them, but they'd have go some to beat this one. It is sharp and precise, a joy to use.<br /><br />The bad: Not a very close shave. I usually suffer irritation, especially on the neck, when using any kind of shaver. This doesn't irritate, but it is probably because it isn't very close. There's no coarseness adjustment, you get what you get. It shaves evenly, just not real close. Also, when I skip a day or two it takes some going over and over to get everything. It does it, just not on one pass. This shaver seems to be fine for daily shaving, it just doesn't seem to handle several-day-old growth well. That may be typical of foil-type shavers, I never noticed it on my rotaries.<br /><br />So-so: There is no protective cover for the foils. There is a hard-side zippered case that form-fits the entire shaver, so maybe the foil cover isn't necessary. The charger cord, however, doesn't fit in the case with the shaver, could present a problem for travelling with it.<br /><br />Summary: A solid, basic shaver for daily use, with a trimmer that's better than most.
  599. I am very satisfied.<br />If i one more buy, i will be buy this one again without no hesitation.

  602. I bought this electric shaver on a whim to replace my [[ASIN:B000UK2VRK Philips Norelco 8040X Moisturizing Shaving System]], which gave me the closest shave I ever had from an electric. The shaving lotion appears to have been discontinued so I was looking into the Braun 7 series. But before I could pull the trigger on the [[ASIN:B004BD8QEO Braun Series 7 Series 7-720S Pulsonic Shaver, Black]], I found the Braun 380S-4 at a good price. I decided to try it out knowing that I could use the 60 day return policy. I like this shaver but there are a few things that could be better. First, the pros.<br /><br />Pros: For the 3-Series (low end model), the shaver does not feel cheap. I've been using the shaver for over a month now and it seems well constructed, although the power button encasing (silver circle around the button) has started making a clicking noise if you touch the top part of the circle. The sensofoil (name of the foil on the 3-Series) does not cause any visible irritation on my skin. This is a huge improvement over the old [[ASIN:B000G1785S Braun Series 5 (8985) Men's Shaver]] (AKA 360 Complete) I used to own which left red marks all over my neck. I even went running immediately after using the 380S and when I returned there was no irritation on my skin, which used to happen all the time with the 360 Complete. I like how I can clean this shaver under the tap like I used to do with my 8040X, something I couldn't do with the 360 Complete. One of the best things about this particular Braun is that it comes with a charging stand, not to be confused with a clean and renew stand. I find this accessory invaluable for those that don't want to have to purchase the cleaning solution to use with the clean and renew stands because the stand allows the shaver to be stored vertically on the bathroom counter, which I think helps with drying. Plus I don't like leaving the shaver laying on the counter. The stand can be used to charge the shaver by plugging thepower cord into the base, but the cord can be plugged directly into the shaver for charging, which is nice if you don't want to bring the stand with you when you go on a trip.<br /><br />Cons: Being that this shaver is the 3-Series, one feature it lacks the \\"Contour Adaptive Shaving Head,\\" which ensures that the shaver foil is always contacting your face at a 90 degree angle, ensuring the most contact between your face and the foils. This feature would be best served when shaving over the jawline, removing the most hair. It also lacks the active lift feature, but on the 360 Complete, that feature was useless. It is supposed to help cut longer hairs that are laying down, moreso than the middle trimmer on the 3-Series shavers. The feature may have improved over the years, but I can't comment on it with the current 7-Series shavers (note: 360 Complete has been retroactively categorized as part of the 5-Series). There are other other features that are not included when compared to the 7-Series that I cannot comment on (pulsonic, sensitivity modes). As far as the shave itself, it does not appear as close as the 8040X, although it is pretty close. The shave will leave patches of stubble, so you will have to go over some areas repeatedly, which costs time but does not really add much irritation.<br /><br />To be honest, if the 720-S came with a charging stand, I would trade in my 380S in a heartbeat. But I confirmed with Braun customer service that the 720-S does not include such a stand. I think that I will stick with the 380S for now, but I am still tempted to try the 7-Series or a high end Panasonic model.
